##

2014-07-03 20:26:37
Sanjana Bhattacharyya
235009
2.5
EDIT: 22 July, 2014

The price has gone up- it is now 357 instead of 321 (A.I.). But the quality is the same as before- in fact, worse than what I had last time actually.

The soup, this time, was way watery and had very little chicken. I loved the crispy fried paneer and the veg crispy wontons but there was a sort of runny curry of corn, potato and bell pepper which was quite bland. The chicken basil wontons were nice, but the problem is that in all that accumulated steam inside the chafing dish, the wonton skin gets soggy and glue-y and not very nice to eat. The crispy chicken was an unmitigated disaster. In fact, if I never visit Haka again, the whole blame is to fall on this dish. The chicken was so tough that I couldn't even manage pierce it with my fork! Not to mention the bones! Some of the pieces were nothing but a row of rickety ribs coated in batter! Most pieces had the meat to batter ratio of 1:2. I wonder if they just gather a pile of unused chicken bits, batter them and serve in the buffet!

The mains had overly garlicky rice and noodles and a decently cooked Chicken Manchurian. In fact, the chicken in this side was rather nice.

The dessert had Monte Carlo, which I liked because of the generous layer of chocolate on top (but I would have liked if the ice cream and the cake was not so icy!). But what was rather shocking is that when the chocolate layer on top of the desert was finished and a few pieces of the cake remained, they refused to refresh the dessert! When we told them that the chocolate was finished and bring a fresh bowl, they simply doused the pieces of cake in chocolate sauce. Appalling!
___________________________________________________________________
When you get over the initial shock of the buffet price (Rs. 321 A.I), you start judging the place by its food and the result is quite disappointing. 

First off, the chicken soup was actually nice, loaded with dark soya sauce. I liked that it was quite salty instead of sweet and sour/hot and sour soups that I am not particularly fond of. However, the itsy bitsy pieces of chicken were scant. The prawn wafers were nice but the crispy noodles were a little hard. Maybe our timing was wrong, maybe the next batch was better.

The starters consisted of a number of vegetarian items and two non-veg. The kimchi was ordinary, the chili mustard potato seemed to be composed of very unlikely flavors that shouldn't be put together. The crispy vegetable parcels (may not be the exact name, but this is what they were) were nice, the batter was thin and crunchy. The crispy, spicy fried vegetables were really good- the batter was thin, crispy and spicy while the vegetables were soft and succulent. However, one tip: load up on these veg when they bring in a fresh batch. Otherwise the crust seems to harden up. The chicken wontons were full of chicken and had a clean, purely chicken-y taste, which I like in wontons. But I wish they had a more fiery sauce to accompany it. The one served that day was nothing more than a sour tomato sauce. The chicken drumsticks of heaven Shandong style were nice, but could do with a slightly thinner coat of batter. 

The main course had one non-veg item, ONE. Why? How? This is beyond disappointment. Even when I had called them, they said they have 2 non-veg items in mains. This is just unacceptable. Even the only chicken item had a weird taste that I didn't like and couldn't eat more than one piece of. I didn't taste the noodles, but I was told that they were just okay. The rice had very little veg in it but was full of dry red chilli, so much so that I couldn't eat more than a couple spoonfuls.

The dessert were surprisingly good. I mean, do not expect the variety of Flame and Grill or BBQ Nation, but the two items they had were quite good. The darsaan was light and crunchy and the mango pastry was very soft and not too sweet. They had chocolate, vanilla and mango flavored ice creams along with chocolate, mint and strawberry sauces.

I hope on my next visit, that is when I go broke again, Haka will have a better buffet spread for me.

3.5
Haka is the cheapest in the Speciality Group of Restaurants. Or rather I can say a cheaper alternative to Mainland China. The outlet at Mani Square has only buffet though I had a-la-carte at its Salt Lake outlet few years back. 

Located inside Mani Square Mall, this place has been frequented by me several times whenever I went shopping or to catch a movie. 

The Buffet has a wide variety of menu and is extremely pocket friendly at about less than 400/- per person on a weekday. The starters are quite soulful. The dimsums too are nice. Steaming hot soup with fried noodles also tastes great. In the main course they give you the option of both trice and noodles. So you can have some of rice with your choice of side dish and then again some noodles with what you feel goes better with it. 

The drawback here is that as many times as I have been there...about 7-8 times...I find the items almost the same. Maybe it has happened so with me. Although I don't really remember all the names but I love their prawn preparation with rice. Everytime I have the biggest portion of this. The foods are all hot and they fill in immediately once it is exhausted.

The dessert part is but heart breaking. Tiny bits of cake and general vanilla, strawberry & chocolate ice cream. Super simple. But anyways what more can you probably expect out if this money, honey?

9. Ice-cream with not so hot chocolate sauce

The only relief were the brownies , small n soft .... and the ice-creams . But , I have serious doubts about the quality of the ingredients used in the preparation .

The buffet is cheap ... so it is pocket friendly for college people . But , still , cannot recommend it !!

3.5
If you are roaming around in Mani Square and are hungry for a value for money Chinese meal, Haka should be your pick. 

The interiors and ambience are okay. The seating though isn't all that comfortable. Although, I have to agree that the food is not bad and the buffet is worth every penny.

The buffet starts with an option on one vegetarian and one non vegetarian soup and some salads along with prawn wafers. All these are good.

Then are are two vegetarian and two non vegetarian appetisers. The cumin potatoes were nothing great. To be honest, they were potato wedges with cumin on top. The wonton was good though. The chicken sim sum was good as well. The chili chicken appetiser wasn't great. 

The main course had and option of rice or noodles. Two vegetarian dishes, and one chicken and one fish dish. The food wasn't bad. But I feel there should have been more variety in terms of the riceand noodles(by keeping a non vegetarian option). The desserts were good. They had an assortment of ice creams, darsaan, pastries, and a pudding.

The food here isn't that great, but if you're in a rush and want some Chinese this is the place to go. I also felt that the service could have been a bit better.

Haka - The most affordable of all the restaurants by the Speciality group.
Haka's cuisine is chinese. It has two outlets : Mani Square (E M Bypass) and City Centre (Salt Lake)

Friend and I went to Haka for an afternoon lunch. I was already sulking because I lost a few bucks to the cab driver and hence now chose to eat at Haka because it was not stingy in the pockets and pretty safe as well.
Haka has an assortment of an entire buffet right from the soup and starters to the desserts at an affordable price of INR 295/- on weekdays and the prices shoot up to INR 345/- on  the weekends.

Amazing isnt it?

So, we started with the soup and the starters. The soup of the day was Chicken sweetcorn soup and had a chicken starter which was spicy and nice and complimented the sweetness of the soup.
The soup was brilliant that day. I took two big helpings of it because I liked it so much.
 Proceeding to the main course, the veg rice that they have is very nice. It has veggies and corn sprinkled all over and is fresh too.
The noodles were butter garlic noodles. Had the slight hotness but the buttery element neutralized it and it tasted good.
There was also a preparation of chicken which tasted good too.

Food is generally good here.
Lastly, the desserts had chocolate cake slices (w/o chocolate sauce), darsaan and ice cream (vanilla, strawberry and chocolate)
I had all three desserts and with a tummyful of food merrily walked out.
An afternoon spent well.

Will be back for more.
cheers! :)

We were a ravenously hungry and moderately poor group of five. Upon entering the enclosed space, going by the name of ‚ÄòHAKA‚Äô, we rarely stopped to think - we only ATE. In retrospect, we took the meaning of ‚Äòall-you-can-eat buffet meals‚Äô to rather shocking levels.

Adorned with all things red, HAKA is neatly and comfortably furnished. We chose the buffet meal service over the a la carte service. The following represent the items that I chose off the available buffet menu:
 (1) Grilled Paneer: Amazing? Check. There was a creamy smoothness to the paneer yet a lingering Tandoori impact of the grilled cooking.
 (2) Spinach Wontons: These gems looked like tea bags. They were slightly crunchy,  terribly delicious and even boasted of a cheese burst in your mouth on some occasions.
 (3) Stir Fried Vegetables: Honestly, it seemed like a consolation dish for the vegetarians - oily and completely unpleasant.
 (4) Chicken Dimsums: Yum yum, to sum up. Soft, delectable and unsparing amounts of chicken in every mouthful!
 (5) Chicken Taipei: In the same league as Chicken Manchurian, this dish, although not boneless, was scrumptious.

There were also chop suey, vegetables tossed in some kind of red sauce, chicken doused in soya sauce and the routine choices of Chow and Fried Rice up for consideration, and the ‚Äòthumbs up‚Äô agreement for all was unanimously taken across our table.

Of the dessert spread, I stuck to Chocolate Cake, several scoops of ice-cream (the available flavours were: chocolate, vanilla, strawberry) and Chocolate Sauce. They were ordinary to taste AND there was not an incredible variety to choose from, which I was ready to forgive on account of offering one of the most affordable buffet meal services.

Charging Rs. 321 a plate including taxes (weekday lunch), it was quite an experience. I deducted half a point because there were several instances of the food on service being cold (also, I wish the chocolate sauce had been served hot) and another half a point for the insufficient choices for the vegetarians.

I plan to revisit as soon as possible and shamelessly gorge as much as possible :D

Craving for Chinese food I decided to visit Haka on a weekend for the lunch buffet.We arrived at around 2:30 and was greeted by the staff with smiling faces.
Now for starters they are now served on the table whereas main course and desserts you have to go and bring.First we had manchow soup which was tasty and with a pinch of sourness.Then we were served with prawn papads which is normal and you can get them at local shops too.The next item (which I loved) was fried chicken wanton, it was crispy with the right amount of chicken,next came the pepper garlic wings which a little sweet yet very delicious.I think this was the item I had the most.For drinks we ordered a pitcher of mango juice with lemon and ginger zest.This was quite refreshing and tasty too.
Coming to main course it was a normal affair with chicken,shrimp and fish side dishes and garlic noodles and chicken fried rice.Since I was nearly stuffed with dessert I took a little rice and shrimp and chicken.Out of these the shrimp tasted the best even though I found the shrimp and chicken preparations were nearly same.
For desserts there was darshan,mousse,cake and ice creams (chocolate,mango and vanilla).I took a little darshan and mousse.The mousse had an unsual peppermint flavour.
The total bill was around 2020 which I would say is quite ok considering the amount of food they provide.Will be back soon for ala carte.

3.5
Haka has been set up to target the budget oriented people and pull them out of their regular food joints. A very spacious room with mediocre decoration but excellent Chinese food - that is exactly how you can summarize Haka; not to forget the comfort of your pocket that is left undisturbed. the buffet generally includes shrimps/prawns in the main course which is definitely a rare sight and the really good quality of those items ensures a positive outcome from the diners. They also present a Chicken Salad and Momo in the starter, and they taste perfect. The staff are warm and service is quite fast. They serve only buffet and no Ala Carte. The dinner buffet priced at 333 AI on weekdays and 380 AI on weekends which i feel is very reasonable. for such place.

I love their clear soup and i find it to be one of the best in town. They have 2-3 salads that are nice. Fried or steamed wantons are pretty good. Apart from them , they have 2 or 3 other starters. Now for the main course vegetables, i find they do not keep their best possible options. I order for a manchurian or a potato and corn in hot garlic beside the buffet that makes it great for me. But the vegetables offered in buffet are not the best i would say and i tend to avoid them in the end. This is the only negative i would point. Deserts options include darsaan which i like and some carrot cakes etc and ice creams which was good enough. 

But in the end the buffet is crazy at its price !!

Pros:
1) Amazing food for that price
2) Comfortable place
3) Warm service

Cons:
1) Decor isn't that grand
2) Main course vegetables aren't that great

After Mainland China's success in Kolkata , Anjan targeted the young & budget minded people to draw them to his no-frill Chinese Restaurant called the Hakka which I admit was an intelligent move on his part & a great success too!Unlike Mainland China , this chain of restaurant has a very simple yet well done interior.I found the attire of the waiters donning  Black & Red,  pretty smart , in fact all his specialty restaurants have a different eye-appeal !This place was a hit & a favourite of  many as the spread offered in the Buffet was simply great compared to the price. I remember having had my first buffet for as little as Rs.165/-plus taxes & was more than satisfied with the food & service ! Of late however the buffet prices have  gone up and those who care for shrimps/prawns , which is generally served on weekends,would  end up paying more, as the spread on weekdays normally  does not include Shrimps/Prawns , even though fish is generally one of the items ! But let me tell you, you will not regret it & if you can really eat well then you are in a win- win situation! A  word of caution........Vegetarians do not have as much choice as Non-Vegetarians ! 

Only one area I feel needs to be considered, that is , the Starters could have some more choice & the desserts should be more &  varied too! I am sure my request would be addressed soon!

2013-08-19 18:20:18
Debdutta Ghosh
1067318
2.5
Haka is owned by the Specialty group and is a junior form of Mainland China. The restaurant provides both A-la-carte and buffet at reasonable prices (cheaper than Mainland China). After a visit to Haka, I was surprised to see the poor quality that Specialty group has come down to.

The food was nowhere near to the tastes of Mainland China. I had my stomach suffer the very next day after having a buffet lunch there. Now this could be just me but I strongly doubt the quality of ingredients used to prepare the food. Going to the menu, nothing out of the ordinary, in fact many items missing from the Mainland China's menu and in the buffet not many options are included.

Moving further to the restaurant, decorations are just about average. The restaurant is decently decorated but they have no false ceiling to cover the air conditioner ducts (at least it was the situation when I visited the restaurant couple of months ago).

To sum up, I don't think that I would recommend anyone to give a visit to Haka till I get some positive reviews about the restaurant and pay another visit. Haka seems to be just a cheaper varient of Mainland China wherein quality of food has been compromised by visible differences.

2013-08-10 08:06:21
Sudip Das
584345
3.5
Having heard quite a lot on the Buffet spread "Haka" offers,  I decided to drop by yesterday.. Please be aware that, though Zomato mentions the dinner timings as 06.30 pm to 11.00 pm, I was surprised when someone outside the place told me, it was actually 7 PM. Then I went there at 07.15 pm again, only to being told to come back after 15 minutes as things were not ready yet.. Hence i have deducted .5 points for that..

Coming to the food now, they had around 12 to 15 items spread out.. I being an "Egg"iterian.. had to go on with stuffs which were marked in green. Started with "Sweet Corn soup" which tasted really nice and thick.. although its tasted really sweet..i had to add some pepper to get the taste i wanted..coming to the starters, In veg, there were, Veg Salad, Aloo Fry(Chinese Aloor Dum i found it to be), Vegetable Fry(Mix of Baby Corn and Potato). Aloo Fry was good..not too oily not too spicy which i liked...Vegetable fry had nothing worth mentioning..just the usual...Then I saw some Vegetabe Dimsums which were OK, followed by Mix Veg Konjenaro and another Veg items(which i cant remember)...this was there along side Hakka Noddles and Fried Rice.. So one gets a chance to have both of these, although i prefer rice anyday over noodles when it comes to a Dinner option.. Neverthelesss, these 2 Veg items contained the same vegetables which irritated me..Cabbage and Cauliflower.. they had these baked one in White sauce and the other one in Soya.. 

After tasting these, I was surprised to see the end of Veg items.. Instead Non Veg items were in contrast more..If you are Non Veg, they offer you the same food only chicken added..and one special item on Shrimps...

For Dessert, I got Darsaan soaked in Honey and one chocolate brownie and Mango crunchy cake...which were the best of the whole lot.. Darsaan would have been better, if they had put some more honey on it...but not bad overall..They also give you a complimentary drink (A Glass of Pepsi) :P

Service was pretty laidback..I was offered a paper napkin and a glass of water.. and the person serving me totally forgot to refill..The decor was OK..nothing to add on except for the fact that the songs were not good AT ALL.. coming to dinner and to have a quite evening.. i never expect some Vengaboys number playing loud on top of me..It might also be that the noise was coming from  "Shack" which was just beside this place..

Cost : 381/- AI for a Weekday Dinner Buffet.  :(

The caramel custard, though not typically a dish I'd associate with chinese food was a treat as were the darsaan with vanilla ice cream. I would strongly recommend the buffet. Way to go!

Haka.. It is located at Mani Square Mall in E M Bypass..
If you go to this place, dont expect a fine dining experience. Or lavish interiors. Or amazing service.  This place is best suited for youngsters, a place to treat a big group or a group of friends who hang out every day & want to sip a drink or two with starters and dont want to spend much. The buffet has very very limited vegetarian options - when I had the buffet they had no eggless desserts available. The food and drinks are very cheap when compared to its peers but we are ready to pay a bit more for better food. The quality and portion of food in a la carte is not bad either but the taste is definitely not as good as other Chinese Restaurants like Mainland China. The service is not great and people are really slow but friendly. One and a half stars from me.

2012-08-31 00:38:19
Bandana Kayal
306104
4.0
If you have a budget constraint yet opt for standard Chinese Lunch/ Dinner there is no better alternative rather than HAKA. I used to visit here once in every month preferably during weekend. Food is not at all rich in preparation but of excellent taste. Ambiance is simple (not overdone) and soothing for family.

With their Low-Priced buffet they seek to attract the younger, quick-meal customers. On the buffet Menu (Weekend Lunch) starters like Crispy Vegetables with Dry Red Chilly, Vegetable Fried Wonton, Chicken Momo and Black Peeper Chicken are offered usually (however they used to change the base sauce and mode of preparation time to time to employ some deviation in taste).  Main course is quite selective with present of delectable items like Burnt Garlic and Corn Fried Rice/ Five-Spiced Fried Rice, Chicken Fried Rice, Hakka Noodles (Veg & Chicken), Chicken in Chilly Oyster Sauce, Fish in Spicy Basil Sauce and Prawn in clear gravy (I can't remember the name). I haven't noticed their vegetable side dish section as I am purely a Non-Veg lover. Shuffling of base sauce is incorporated for main course menu as well.

The meal is accompanied by 2 soups (vegetable and chicken), Crispy Noodles, Prawn Wafers and 2-3 varieties of Salad (don't miss chicken one). Their desert section is not satisfactory, it is concise and I haven't found good Ice-Cream even for a single occasion in subsequent visit. Beverages are available on demand. Try to avoid alcoholic drinks; these are really very costly rather you may settle with Mocktails. Their service is fast and staffs are quite attentive.  They have an √† la carte menu too but it has few takers.
